I PETER RABBIT BECOMES ACQUAINTED WITH MRS. QUACK Make a new acquaintance every time you can ; You 'll find it interesting and a very helpful plan .
It mean more knowledge .
You can not meet any one without learn something from him if you keep your ear open and your eye open .
Every one be at least a little different from every one else , and the more people you know , the more you may learn .
Peter Rabbit know this , and that be one reason he always be so eager to find out about other people .
He have leave Jimmy Skunk and Bobby Coon in the Green Forest and have head for the Smiling Pool to see if Grandfather Frog be awake yet .
He have no idea of meet a stranger there , and so you can imagine just how surprised he be when he get in sight of the Smiling Pool to see some one whom he never have see before swim about there .
He know right away who it be .
He know that it be Mrs. Quack the Duck , because he have often hear about her .
And then , too , it be very clear from her look that she be a cousin of the duck he have see in Farmer Brown 's dooryard .
The difference be that while they be big and white and stupid-looking , Mrs. Quack be small , brown , very trim , and look anything but stupid .
Peter be so surprised to see her in the Smiling Pool that he almost forget to be polite .
I be afraid he star in a very impolite way a he hurry to the edge of the bank .
`` I suppose , '' say Peter , `` that you be Mrs. Quack , but I never expect to see you unless I should go over to the Big River , and that be a place I never have visit and hardly expect to because it be too far from the dear Old Briar-patch .
You be Mrs. Quack , be n't you ? ''
`` Yes , '' reply Mrs. Quack , `` and you must be Peter Rabbit .
I 've hear of you very often . ''
All the time Mrs. Quack be swim back and forth and in little circle in the most uneasy way .
`` I hope you 've hear nothing but good of me , '' reply Peter .
Mrs. Quack stop her uneasy swim for a minute and almost smile a she look at Peter , `` The bad I have hear be that you be very curious about other people 's affair , '' say she .
Peter look a wee , wee bit foolish , and then he laugh right out .
`` I guess that be true enough , '' say he .
`` I like to learn all I can , and how can I learn without be curious ?
I 'm curious right now .
I 'm wonder what bring you to the Smiling Pool when you never have be here before .
It be the last place in the world I ever expect to find you . ''
`` That 's why I 'm here , '' reply Mrs. Quack .
`` I hope others feel the same way .
I come here because I just HAD to find some place where people would n't expect to find me and so would n't come look for me .
Little Joe Otter saw me yesterday on the Big River and tell me of this place , and so , because I just have to go somewhere , I come here . ''
Peter 's eye open very wide with surprise .
`` Why , '' he exclaim , `` I should think you would be perfectly safe on the Big River !
I do n't see how any harm can possibly come to you out there . ''
The word be no sooner out of Peter 's mouth than a faint bang sound from way off towards the Big River .
Mrs. Quack give a great start and half lift her wing a if to fly .
But she think good of it , and then Peter saw that she be tremble all over .
`` Did you hear that ? ''
she ask in a faint voice .
Peter nod .
`` That be a gun , a terrible gun , but it be a long way from here , '' say he .
`` It be over on the Big River , '' say Mrs. Quack .
`` That 's why it be n't safe for me over there .
That 's why I just have to find some other place .
Oh , dear , the very sound of a gun set me to shake and make my heart feel a if it would stop beating .
Are you sure I be perfectly safe here ? ''
`` Perfectly , '' speak up Jerry Muskrat , who have be listen from the top of the Big Rock , where he be lunch on a clam , `` unless you be not smart enough to keep out of the clutch of Reddy Fox or Old Man Coyote or Hooty the Owl or Redtail the Hawk . ''
`` I 'm not afraid of THEM , '' declare Mrs. Quack .
`` It 's those two-legged creature with terrible gun I 'm afraid of , '' and she begin to swim about more uneasily than ever .
II MRS. QUACK IS DISTRUSTFUL Jerry Muskrat think there be no place in the world like the Smiling Pool .
So , for the matter of that , do Grandfather Frog and also Spotty the Turtle .
You see , they have spend their life there and know little about the rest of the Great World .
When Mrs. Quack explain that all she fear be that a two-legged creature with a terrible gun might find her there , Jerry Muskrat hasten to tell her that she have nothing to worry about on that account .
`` No one hunt here now that Farmer Brown 's boy have put away his terrible gun , '' explain Jerry .
`` There be a time when he use to hunt here and set trap , which be bad than terrible gun , but that be long ago , before he know any good . ''
`` Who be Farmer Brown 's boy ? ''
demand Mrs. Quack , look more anxious than ever .
`` Is he one of those two-legged creature ? ''
`` Yes , '' say Peter Rabbit , who have be listen with all his ear , `` but he be the best friend we Quaddies have get .
He be such a good friend that he ought to be a Quaddy himself .
Why , this last winter he feed some of u when food be scarce , and he save Mrs. Grouse when she be catch in a snare , which you know be a kind of trap .
He wo n't let any harm come to you here , Mrs. Quack . ''
`` I would n't trust him , not for one single little minute , '' declare Mrs. Quack .
`` I would n't trust one of those two-legged creature , not ONE .
You say he feed some of you last winter , but that do n't mean anything good .
Do you know what I 've know these two-legged creature to do ? ''
`` What ? ''
demand Peter and Jerry together .
`` I 've know them to scatter food where we Ducks would be sure to find it and to take the great care that nothing should frighten u while we be eat .
And then , after we have get in the habit of feed in that particular place and have grow to feel perfectly safe there , they have hide close by until a lot of u be feed together and then fire their terrible gun and kill a lot of my friend and dreadfully hurt a lot more .
I would n't trust one of them , not ONE ! ''
`` Oh , how dreadful ! ''
cry Peter , look quite as shocked a he felt .
Then he add eagerly , `` But our Farmer Brown 's boy would n't do anything like that .
You have n't the least thing to fear from him . ''
`` Perhaps not , '' say Mrs. Quack , shake her head doubtfully , `` but I would n't trust him .
I would n't trust him a far off a I could see him .
The Smiling Pool be a very nice place , although it be dreadfully small , but if Farmer Brown 's boy be likely to come over here , I guess I good look for some other place , though goodness know where I will find one where I will feel perfectly safe . ''
`` You be safe right here , if you have sense enough to stay here , '' declare Jerry Muskrat rather testily .
`` Do n't you suppose Peter and I know what we be talk about ? ''
`` I wish I could believe so , '' return Mrs. Quack sadly , `` but if you have be through what I 've be through , and suffer what I 've suffer , you would n't believe any place safe , and you certainly would n't trust one of those two-legged creature .
Why , for week they have n't give me a chance to get a square meal , and -- and -- I do n't know what have become of Mr. Quack , and I 'm all alone ! ''
There be a little sob in her voice and tear in her eye .
`` Tell u all about it , '' beg Peter .
`` Perhaps we can help you . ''
III MRS. QUACK TELLS ABOUT HER HOME `` It 's a long story , '' say Mrs. Quack , shake the tear from her eye , `` and I hardly know where to begin . ''
`` Begin at the beginning , '' say Jerry Muskrat .
`` Your home be somewhere way up in the Northland where Honker the Goose life , be n't it ? ''
Mrs. Quack nod .
`` I wish I be there this very minute , '' she reply , the tear come again .
`` But sometimes I doubt if ever I 'll get there again .
You folk who do n't have to leave your home every year do n't know how well off you be or how much you have to be thankful for . ''
`` I never could understand what people want to leave their home for , anyway , '' declare Peter .
`` We do n't leave because we want to , but because we HAVE to , '' reply Mrs. Quack , `` and we go back just as soon a we can .
What would you do if you could n't find a single thing to eat ? ''
`` I guess I 'd starve , '' reply Peter simply .
`` I guess you would , and that be just what we would do , if we do n't take the long journey south when Jack Frost freeze everything tight up there where my home be , '' return Mrs. Quack .
`` He come early up there and stay twice as long a he do here , and make ten time as much ice and snow .
We get most of our food in the water or in the mud under the water , a of course you know , and when the water be frozen , there be n't a scrap of anything we can get to eat .
We just HAVE to come south .
It be n't because we want to , but because we must !
There be nothing else for u to do . ''
`` Then I do n't see what you want to make your home in such a place for , '' say practical Peter .
`` I should think you would make it where you can live all the year around . ''
`` I be bear up there , and I love it just a you love the dear Old Briar-patch , '' reply Mrs. Quack simply .
`` It be home , and there be no place like home .
Besides , it be a very beautiful and a very wonderful place in summer .
There be everything that Ducks and Geese love .
We have all we want of the food we love best .
Everywhere be shallow water with tall grass grow in it . ''
`` Huh ! ''
interrupt Peter , `` I would n't think much of a place like that . ''
`` That 's because you do n't know what be good , '' snap Jerry Muskrat .
`` It would suit me , '' he add , with shin eye .
`` There be the dear little island just make for safe nesting-places , '' continue Mrs. Quack , without heed the interruption .
`` And the day be long , and it be easy to hide , and there be nothing to fear , for two-legged creature with terrible gun never come there . ''
`` If there be nothing to fear , why do you care about place to hide ? ''
demand Peter .
`` Well , of course , we have enemy , just a you do here , but they be natural enemy , -- Foxes and Minks and Hawks and Owls , '' explain Mrs. Quack .
`` Of course , we have to watch out for them and have place where we can hide from them , but it be our wit against their wit , and it be our own fault if we get catch .
That be perfectly fair , so we do n't mind that .
It be only men who be not fair .
They do n't know what fairness be . ''
Peter nod that he understand , and Mrs. Quack go on .
`` Last summer Mr. Quack and I have our nest on the dear little island , and no one find it .
First we have twelve egg , and then twelve of the dear baby you ever saw . ''
`` Maybe , '' say Peter doubtfully , think of his own baby .
`` They grow so fast that by the time the cold weather come , they be as big a their father and mother , '' continue Mrs. Quack .
`` And they be smart , too .
They have learn how to take care of themselves just as well a I could .
I certainly be proud of that family .
But now I do n't know where one of them be . ''
Mrs. Quack suddenly choke up with grief , and Peter Rabbit politely turn his head away .
IV MRS. QUACK CONTINUES HER STORY When Mrs. Quack told of her twelve child and how she do n't know where one of them be , Peter Rabbit and Jerry Muskrat know just how badly she be feel , and they turn their head away and pretend that they do n't see her tear .
In a few minute she bravely go on with her story .
`` When Jack Frost come and we know it be time to begin the long journey , Mr. Quack and myself and our twelve child join with some other Duck family , and with Mr. Quack in the lead , we start for our winter home , which really be n't a home but just a place to stay .
For a while we have nothing much to fear .
We would fly by day and at night rest in some quiet lake or pond or on some river , with the Great Woods all about u or sometimes great marsh .
Perhaps you do n't know what marsh be .
If the Green Meadows here have little stream of water run every which way through them , and the ground be all soft and muddy and full of water , and the grass grow tall , they would be marsh . ''
Jerry Muskrat 's eye sparkle .
`` I would like a place like that ! ''
he exclaim .
`` You certainly would , '' reply Mrs. Quack .
`` We always find lot of your relative in such place . ''
`` Marshes must be something like swamp , '' venture Peter Rabbit , who have be think the matter over .
`` Very much the same , only with grass and rush in place of tree and bush , '' reply Mrs. Quack .
`` There be plenty to eat and the lovely hiding-places .
In some of these we stay day at a time .
In fact , we stay until Jack Frost come to drive u out .
Then a we fly , we begin to see the home of these terrible two-legged creature call men , and from that time on we never know a minute of peace , except when we be fly high in the air or far out over the water .
If we could have just keep fly all the time or never have to go near the shore , we would have be all right .
But we have to eat . ''
`` Of course , '' say Peter .
`` Everybody have to eat . ''
`` And we have to rest , '' say Mrs. Quack .
`` Certainly , '' say Peter .
`` Everybody have to do that . ''
`` And to eat we have to go in close to shore where the water be not at all deep , because it be only in such place that we can get food , '' continue Mrs. Quack .
`` It take a lot of strength to fly a we fly , and strength require plenty of food .
Mr. Quack know all the best feeding-places , for he have make the long journey several time , so every day he would lead the way to one of these .
He always choose the wild and most lonely look place he could find , as far a possible from the home of men , but even then he be never careless .
He would lead u around back and forth over the place he have choose , and we would all look with all our might for sign of danger .
If we saw none , we would drop down a little nearer and a little nearer .
But with all our watchfulness , we never could be sure , absolutely sure , that all be safe .
Sometimes those terrible two-legged creature would be hide in the very middle of the wild , most lonely look marsh .
They would be cover with grass so that we could n't see them .
Then , a we fly over them , would come the bang , bang , bang , bang of terrible gun , and always some of our flock would drop .
We would have to leave them behind , for we know if we want to live we must get beyond the reach of those terrible gun .
So we would fly our hardest .
It be awful , just simply awful ! ''
Mrs. Quack pause and shudder , and Peter Rabbit and Jerry Muskrat shudder in sympathy .
`` Sometimes we would have to try three or four feeding-places before we find one where there be no terrible gun .
And when we do find one , we would be so tired and frighten that we could n't enjoy our food , and we do n't dare to sleep without some one on watch all the time .
It be like that every day .
The farther we get , the bad it become .
Our flock grow small and small .
Those who escape the terrible gun would be so frightened that they would forget to follow their leader and would fly in different direction and later perhaps join other flock .
So it be that when at last we reach the place in the sunny Southland for which we have start , Mr. Quack and I be alone .
What become of our twelve child I do n't know .
I be afraid the terrible gun kill some .
I hope some join other flock and escape , but I do n't know . ''
`` I hope they do too , '' say Peter .
V PETER LEARNS MORE OF MRS. QUACK 'S TROUBLES It often happen when we know The trouble that our friend pass through , Our own seem very small indeed ; You 'll always find that this be true .
`` My , you must have felt glad when you reach your winter home ! ''
exclaim Peter Rabbit when Mrs. Quack finish the account of her long , terrible journey from her summer home in the far Northland to her winter home in the far Southland .
`` I do , '' reply Mrs. Quack , `` but all the time I could n't forget those to whom terrible thing have happen on the way down , and then , too , I keep dread the long journey back . ''
`` I do n't see why you do n't stay right there .
I would have , '' say Peter , nod his head with an air of great wisdom .
`` Not if you be I , '' reply Mrs. Quack .
`` In the first place it be n't a proper place in which to bring up young Ducks and make them strong and healthy .
In the second place there be more danger down there for young Ducks than up in the far Northland .
In the third place there be n't room for all the Ducks to nest properly .
And lastly there be a great longing for our real home , which Old Mother Nature have put in our heart and which just MAKES u go .
We could n't be happy if we do n't . ''
`` Is the journey back as bad a the journey down ? ''
ask Peter .
`` Worse , very much bad , '' reply Mrs. Quack sadly .
`` You can see for yourself just how bad it be , for here I be all alone . ''
Tears fill Mrs. Quack 's eye .
`` It be almost too terrible to talk about , '' she continue after a minute .
`` You see , for one thing , food be n't as plentiful a it be in the fall , and we just have to go wherever it be to be find .
Those two-legged creature know where those feeding-grounds be just as well a we do , and they hide there with their terrible gun just a they do when we be come south .
But it be much bad now , very much bad .
You see , when we be go the other way , if we find them at one place we could go on to another , but when we be go north we can not always do that .
We can not go any fast than Jack Frost do .
Sometimes we be drive out of a place by the bang , bang of the terrible gun and go on , only to find that we have catch up with Jack Frost , and that the pond and the river be still cover with ice .
Then there be nothing to do but to turn back to where those terrible gun be wait for u .
We just HAVE to do it . ''
Mrs. Quack stop and shiver .
`` It seem to me I have hear nothing but the noise of those terrible gun ever since we start , '' say she .
`` I have n't have a good square meal for day and day , nor a good rest .

We would just have to drop into one of these to rest a little , because we have fly so far that our wing ache a if they would drop off .
Then just a we would think we be safe for a little while , there would come the bang of a terrible gun .
Then we would have to fly again as long a we could , and finally come back to the same place because there be no other place where we could go .
Then we would have to do it all over again until night come .
Sometimes I think that those men with terrible gun must hate u and want to kill every one of u .

They simply have n't any heart at all . ''

`` But wait until you know Farmer Brown 's boy !
HE 'S get a heart ! ''
he add brightly .
`` I do n't want to know him , '' retort Mrs. Quack .
`` If he come near here , you 'll see me leave in a hurry .

You do n't think he will come , do you ? ''
Peter sit up and look across the Green Meadows , and his heart sank .
`` He 's come now , but I 'm sure he wo n't hurt you , Mrs. Quack , '' say he .
But Mrs. Quack would n't wait to see .
With a hasty promise to come back when the way be clear , she jump into the air and on swift wing disappear towards the Big River .
VI FARMER BROWN 'S BOY VISITS THE SMILING POOL Farmer Brown 's boy have hear Welcome Robin singing in the Old Orchard quite as soon a Peter Rabbit have , and that song of `` Cheer up !
Cheer up !
Cheer up !
Cheer ! ''
have awaken quite as much gladness in his heart a it have in Peter 's heart .
It mean that Mistress Spring really have arrive , and that over in the Green Forest and down on the Green Meadows there would soon be shy blue , and just a shy white violet to look for , and other flower almost if not quite a sweet and lovely .
It mean that his feathered friend would soon be busy house-hunting and building .
It mean that his little friend in fur would also be do something very similar , if they have not already do so .
It mean that soon there would be a million lovely thing to see and a million joyous sound to hear .
So the sound of Welcome Robin 's voice make the heart of Farmer Brown 's boy even more happy than it be before , and a Welcome Robin just HAD to sing , so Farmer Brown 's boy just HAD to whistle .
When his work be finish , it seem to Farmer Brown 's boy that something be call him , call him to get out on the Green Meadows or over in the Green Forest and share in the happiness of all the little people there .

Farmer Brown 's boy have guess exactly right , a you and I know , and a Peter Rabbit and Jerry Muskrat know .
`` It 's a shame , a downright shame that any one should want to shoot bird on their way to their nesting-grounds and that the law should let them if they do want to .

He grin at the idea , and then he continue his way towards the Smiling Pool .

`` Hello , Jerry Muskrat ! ''
say he .

`` I know what I 'll do .
I 'll go straight back home and get some wheat and corn and put it here on the edge of the Smiling Pool .
Perhaps she will come back and find it . ''

VII MRS. QUACK RETURNS Peter Rabbit just could n't go back to the dear Old Briar-patch .
He just HAD to know if Mrs. Quack would come back to the Smiling Pool .

But he could n't blame her , after all she have be through .
So he keep still and wait .
He be learn , be Peter Rabbit .

VIII MRS. QUACK HAS A GOOD MEAL AND A REST There 's nothing like a stomach full To make the heart feel light ; To chase away the cloud of care And make the world seem bright .
That 's a fact .
A full stomach make the whole world seem different , brighter , good , and more worth living in .
It be the hard kind of hard work to be cheerful and see only the bright side of thing when your stomach be empty .
But once fill that empty stomach , and everything be change .
It be just that way with Mrs. Quack .
For day at a time she have n't have a full stomach because of the hunter with their terrible gun , and when just before dark that night she return to the Smiling Pool , her stomach be quite empty .
`` I do n't suppose I 'll find much to eat here , but a little in peace and safety be good than a feast with worry and danger , '' say she , swim over to the brown , broken-down bulrush on one side of the Smiling Pool and appear to stand on her head a she plunge it under water and search in the mud on the bottom for food .

IX PETER RABBIT MAKES AN EARLY CALL Peter Rabbit be so full of interest in Mrs. Quack and her trouble that he be back at the Smiling Pool before Mr. Sun have kick off his rosy blanket and begin his daily climb up in the blue , blue sky .

But he do n't .
He keep perfectly still .

That be , she carefully put back in place every feather that have be rumple up .
She take a great deal of time for this , for Mrs. Quack be very neat and tidy and take the great pride in look as fine a she can .

He do n't mean to be impolite .

You know Peter do n't waste any time on his clothes .

Finally Peter hop to the edge of the bank where she would see him .

`` That 's a good name for it , '' return Mrs. Quack .

Peter felt tear of sympathy in his own eye .

he ask .

X HOW MR. AND MRS. QUACK STARTED NORTH Peter Rabbit be eager to help Mrs. Quack in her trouble , though he have n't the least idea how he could help and neither have she .

He be give her his sympathy , and sympathy often help others a great deal more than we even guess .
It sometimes be a very good plan to tell your trouble to some one who will listen with sympathy .
It be so with Mrs. Quack .
She have keep her trouble lock in her own heart so long that it do her good to pour them all out to Peter .
`` Mr. Quack and I spend a very comfortable winter way down in the sunny Southland , '' say she with a far-away look .

Of course , we have to have our wit with u all the time , because there be Hawks and Owls and Minks down there just a there be up here , but any Duck who ca n't keep out of their way deserve to furnish one of them a dinner .
`` Then there be another fellow we have to watch out for , a queer fellow whom we never see anywhere but down there .

`` What 's that ? ''
Peter Rabbit lean forward and star at Mrs. Quack with his eye pop right out .
`` What 's that ? ''
he repeat .
`` How can an old log have a mouth ? ''
Mrs. Quack just have to smile , Peter be so in earnest and look so astonished .

Then , too , he will swim under water and come up underneath and seize you without any warning .
He have the big mouth I 've ever see , with terrible-looking teeth , and could swallow me whole . ''

By this time Peter 's eye look a if they would fall out of his head .

whisper Peter .

We live quietly and try to get in as good condition a possible for the long journey back to our home in the North .
When it be time to start , a lot of u get together , just a we do when we come down from the North , only this time the young Ducks felt themselves quite grow up .
In fact , before we start there be a great deal of love-making , and each one choose a mate .
That be a very happy time , a very happy time indeed , but it be a sad time too for u old Ducks , because we know what dreadful thing be likely to happen on the long journey .

Mrs. Quack 's eye suddenly fill with tear again .
`` Oh , dear , '' she sob , `` I wish I know what become of Mr. Quack . ''

Presently Mrs. Quack go on with her story .
`` We have a splendid big flock when we start , make up wholly of pair , each pair dreaming of the home they would build when they reach the far North .

Mr. Quack lead u to the safest feeding and rest ground he know of , and for a time our flock escape the terrible gun .
But the farther we go , the more gun there be . ''

XI THE TERRIBLE , TERRIBLE GUNS `` Bang !
Bang !
Bang !
Not a feather spare !
Kill !
Kill !
Kill !
Wound and rip and tear ! ''
That be what the terrible gun roar from morning to night at Mrs. Quack and her friend a they fly on their long journey to their home in the far North .
I do n't wonder that she be terribly uneasy and nervous a she sit in the Smiling Pool talk to Peter Rabbit ; do you ?
`` Yes , '' say she , continue her story of her long journey from the sunny Southland where she have spend the winter , `` the farther we get , the more there be of those terrible gun .

The very safest-looking place sometimes be the most dangerous .
If you saw a lot of Rabbits play together on the Green Meadows , you would feel perfectly safe in join them , would n't you ? ''
Peter nod .
`` I certainly would , '' say he .
`` If it be safe for them it certainly would be safe for me . ''
`` Well , that be just the way we felt when we saw a lot of Ducks swim about on the edge of one of those feeding-places .

So we go straight in to join those Ducks , and then , just a we set our wing to drop down on the water among them , there be a terrible bang , bang , bang , bang !
My heart almost stop beating .
Then how we do fly !
When we be far out over the water where we could see that nothing be near u we stop to rest , and there we find only half a many in our flock a there have be . ''
`` Where be the others ? ''
ask Peter , although he guess .
`` Killed or hurt by those terrible gun , '' reply Mrs. Quack sadly .
`` And that be n't the bad of it .
I tell you that when we start each of u have a mate .

They be heartbroken .
When it come time for u to move on , they would n't go .
They say that if they do reach the nesting-place in the far North , they could n't have nest or egg or young because they have no mate , so what be the use ?
Besides , they hop that if they wait around they might find their mate .
They think they might not have be kill , but just hurt , and might be able to get away from those hunter .
So they leave u and swim back towards that terrible place , call for their lose mate , and it be the sad sound .
I know now just how they felt , for I have lose Mr. Quack , and that 's why I 'm here . ''

`` But what happen to those Ducks that be swim about there and make you think it be safe ? ''
ask Peter , with a puzzled look on his face .
`` Nothing , '' reply Mrs. Quack .
`` They have be fasten out there in the water by the hunter so a to make u think it safe , and the terrible gun be fire at u and not at them .

Peter blink his eye rapidly a if he be have hard work to believe what he have be tell .
`` Why , '' say be at last , `` I never heard of anything so dreadfully unfair in all my life !

`` That 's just what I mean , '' return Mrs. Quack .
`` Those two-legged creature do n't know what fairness be .
Why , some of them have learn our language and actually call u in where they can shoot u .
Just think of that !
They tell u in our own language that there be plenty to eat and all be safe , so that we will think that other Ducks be hidden and feed there , and then when we go to join them , we be shoot at !
You ought to be mighty thankful , Peter Rabbit , that you be not a Duck . ''
`` I be , '' reply Peter .
He know that not one of the meadow and forest people who be always try to catch him would do a thing like that .
`` It 's all true , '' say Mrs. Quack , `` and those hunter do other thing just a unfair .
Sometimes awful storm will come up , and we just have to find place where we can rest .
Those hunter will hide near those place and shoot at u when we be so tired that we can hardly move a wing .
It would n't be so bad if a hunter would be satisfy to kill just one Duck , just a Reddy Fox be , but he seem to want to kill EVERY Duck .
Foxes and Hawks and Owls catch a good many young Ducks , just a they do young Rabbits , but you know how we feel about that .
They only hunt when they be hungry , and they hunt fairly .
When , they have get enough to make a dinner , they stop .
They keep our wit sharp .
If we do not keep out of their way , it be our own fault .
It be a kind of game -- the game of life .
I guess it be Old Mother Nature 's way of keep u wide-awake and sharpen our wit , and so make u well fit to live .
`` With these two-legged creature with terrible gun , it be all different .
We do n't have any chance at all .
If they hunt u a Reddy Fox do , try to catch u themselves , it would be different .
But their terrible gun kill when we be a long way off , and there be n't any way for u to know of the danger .
And then , when one of them do kill a Duck , he be n't satisfied , but keep on kill and kill and kill .
I 'm sure one would make him a dinner , if that be what he want .
`` And they often simply break the wing or otherwise terribly hurt the one they shoot at , and then leave them to suffer , unable to take care of themselves .
Oh , dear , I 'm afraid that be what have happen to Mr. Quack . ''
Once more poor Mrs. Quack be quite overcome with her trouble and sorrow .
Peter wish with all his heart that he could do something to comfort her , but of course he could n't , so he just sit still and wait until she could tell him just what do happen to Mr. Quack .
XII WHAT DID HAPPEN TO MR. QUACK `` When do you last see Mr. Quack ? ''

But we do , and neither Mr. Quack nor I have lose a feather from those terrible gun that have bang at u all the way up and that have kill so many of our friend .

XV THE HUNT FOR MR. QUACK In spite of her hopelessness in regard to Mr. Quack , there be no doubt that Mrs. Quack felt well that night after she have eat the corn leave among the rush of the Smiling Pool by Farmer Brown 's boy .

It mean the power to make yourself do a certain thing , no matter how much you may want to do something else .

XVIII SAMMY JAY SENDS MRS. QUACK TO THE SWAMP When Sammy Jay leave Mr. Quack in the swamp over by the bank of the Big River , he fly straight back to the Smiling Pool .

While they wait for Mrs. Quack he tell how he have hunt and hunt along the farther bank of the Big River and how he have see the hunter with their terrible gun hiding and have warn Mrs. Quack just where each one be .
Jolly , round , red Mr. Sun be get ready to go to bed behind the Purple Hills and the Black Shadows be begin to creep out over the Green Meadows before Mrs. Quack come .
In fact , Sammy Jay and Blacky be get very uneasy .
It be almost bed-time for them , for neither of them dare stay out after dark .
They have almost make up their mind to leave Peter to tell the news when they saw Mrs. Quack come swiftly from the direction of the Big River .
She look so sad and discourage that even Blacky the Crow be sorry for her , and you know Blacky be n't much give to such feeling .
`` What 's the news , Mrs. Quack ? ''
ask Peter , his eye dance .
`` There be n't any , '' reply Mrs. Quack .
`` Oh , yes , there be ! ''
cry Sammy Jay , who could n't possibly keep still any longer .
`` What be it ? ''
demand Mrs. Quack eagerly , and it seem to Peter that there be a wee bit of hope in her voice .
`` Did you happen to notice that just before the Laughing Brook join the Big River it flow through a little swamp ? ''
ask Sammy .
Mrs. Quack nod her head rapidly .
`` What of it ? ''
she demand .
`` Nothing much , only if I be you I would go down there after dark , '' reply Sammy .
Mrs. Quack look up at Sammy sharply .
`` Why should I go down there ? ''
she ask .
`` If I tell you , will you wait until I get quite through ? ''
ask Sammy in his turn .
Mrs. Quack promise that she would .
`` Well , then , '' reply Sammy , `` this afternoon I find a stranger hiding in there , a stranger with a beautiful green head and neck and a white collar . ''
`` Mr. Quack !
Oh , it be Mr. Quack ! ''
cried Mrs. Quack joyfully and lift her wing a if she would start for the swamp at once .
`` Stop ! ''
cry Sammy sharply .
`` You say you would wait until I be through .
It wo n't do for you to go there until after dark , because there be a hunter hide very near Mr. Quack 's hiding-place .
Wait until it be dark and he have go home .
Then take my advice , and when you have find Mr. Quack , bring him right up here to the Smiling Pool .
He ca n't fly , but he can swim up the Laughing Brook , and this be the safe place for both of you .
Now good night and good luck . ''
XIX JERRY MUSKRAT 'S GREAT IDEA A friendly friend be a friend indeed When he prove a friend in the time of need .
Mr. and Mrs. Quack have be so much take up with each other and with their trouble that they have quite forget they be not alone in the Smiling Pool , which they have reach by swim up the Laughing Brook .
So it happen that when Mrs. Quack suggest that if Mr. Quack 's wing get strong they might be able to find a lonesome pond not too far away where they could make their home for the summer , they be a little startled to hear a voice say : `` I know where there be one , and you will not have to fly at all to get to it . ''
Both jump a little .
You see their nerve have be very much upset for a long time , and the least unexpected thing make them jump .
Then both laugh .
`` Hello , Jerry Muskrat !
We 'd forget all about you , '' say Mrs. Quack .
`` What be that you say ? ''
Jerry good-naturedly repeat what he have say .
Mrs. Quack 's face brighten .
`` Do you really mean it ? ''
she ask eagerly .
`` Do you really mean that you know of a pond where we could live and not be likely to be see by these two-legged creature call men ? ''
`` That 's what I say , '' reply Jerry briefly .
`` Oh , Jerry , you 're not joking , be you ?
Tell me you 're not joke , '' beg Mrs. Quack .
`` Of course I 'm not joke , '' return Jerry just a little bit indignantly , `` I be not the kind of a fellow to joke people who be in such trouble a you and Mr. Quack seem to be in .
The idea come to me while you be talk .
I could n't help overhear what you be say , and the minute you mention a lonesome pond , the idea come to me , and I think it 's a perfectly splendid idea .
I know of just the lonesome kind of a lonesome pond , and you wo n't have to fly a stroke to get to it .
If you be smart enough not to be catch by Reddy Fox or Hooty the Owl or Billy Mink or any of those people who hunt for a living , there be n't any reason I know of why you should n't spend the summer there in peace and comfort . ''
Mrs. Quack 's eye fairly shine with hope and eagerness .
`` Oh , Jerry , tell u where it be , and we 'll start for it right away ! ''
she cry .
Jerry 's eye twinkle .
`` Of course , the owner of that pond might not like to have neighbor .
I have n't think of that , '' say he .
`` Perhaps he ought to be ask first . ''
Mrs. Quack 's face fell .
`` Who be the owner ? ''
she ask .
`` My cousin , Paddy the Beaver .
He make it , '' reply Jerry proudly .
Mrs. Quack 's face light up again at once .
`` I 'm sure he wo n't object , '' say she .
`` We know a great many of the Beaver family .
In fact , they be very good neighbor of ours in our home in the far Northland .
I do n't suppose there be a Beaver pond anywhere around here .
Tell me where it be , Jerry , and I 'll go right up there and call on your cousin . ''
`` All you 've get to do be to follow the Laughing Brook way back into the Green Forest , and you 'll come to Paddy 's pond , '' say he .
`` He make that pond himself two year ago .
He come down from the Great Woods and build a dam across the Laughing Brook way back there in the Green Forest and give u a great scare here in the Smiling Pool by cut off the water for a few day .
He have get a very nice pond there now .
Honker the Goose and his flock spend a night in it on their way south last fall . ''
Mrs. Quack wait to hear no more .
She shoot up into the air and disappear over the top of the tree in the Green Forest .
`` What do you think of my idea ? ''
ask Jerry , a he and Mr. Quack watch her out of sight .
`` I think it be great , just simply great , '' reply Mr. Quack .
XX HAPPY DAYS FOR MR. AND MRS. QUACK Whose heart be true and brave and strong , Who ne'er give up to grim despair , Will find some day that sky be blue And all the world be bright and fair .
If you do n't believe it , just ask Mr. and Mrs. Quack .
They know .
Certainly the world never look darker for any one than it do for them when the terrible gun of a hunter break Mr. Quack 's wing on the Big River and end all their dream of a home in the far Northland .
Then , through the help of Jerry Muskrat , they find the lonely pond of Paddy the Beaver deep in the Green Forest , and there , because their secret have be well keep , presently they find peace and hope and then happiness .
You see , the heart of Mrs. Quack be true and brave and strong .
She be the kind to make the best of thing , and she at once decide that if they could n't have their home where they want it , they would have it where they could have it .
She be determine that they should have a home anyway , and Paddy the Beaver 's little pond be not such a bad place after all .
So she waste no time .
She examine every inch of the shore of that little pond .
At last , a little back from the water , she find a place to suit her , a place so well hide by bush that only the sharp eye ever would find it .
And a little late it would be still harder to find , a she well know , for all about clump of tall fern be spring up , and when they have fully unfold , not even the keen eye of Sammy Jay look down from a near-by tree would be able to discover her secret .
There she make a nest on the ground , a nest of dried grass and leaf , and line it with the softest and most beautiful of lining , down pluck from her own breast .
In it she lay ten egg .
Then come long week of patient sit on them , watch the wonder of grow thing about her , the bursting into bloom of shy wood flower , the unfolding of leaf on bush and tree , the spring up in a night of queer mushroom , which people call toadstool , and all the time dream beautiful Duck dream of the baby which would one day hatch from those precious egg .
She never leave them save to get a little food and just enough exercise to keep her well and strong , and when she do leave them , she always carefully pull soft down over them to keep them warm while she be away .
Mr. Quack know all about that nest , though he have take no part in build it and have no share in the care of those egg .
He be very willing that she should do all the work and think it quite sufficient that he should be on guard to give warning if danger should appear .
So he spend the long beautiful day lazily swim about in the little pond , gossip with Paddy the Beaver , and take the best of care of himself .
The broken wing heal and grow strong again , for it have not be so badly break , after all .
If he miss the company of others of his kind which he would have have during these long day of wait have they be able to reach their usual nesting-place in the far Northland , he never mention it .
Unknown to them , Farmer Brown 's boy discover where they be .
Later he come often to the pond and be content to sit quietly on the shore and watch Mr. Quack , so that Mr. Quack grow quite use to him and do not fear him at all .
In fact , after the first few time , he make no attempt to hide .
You see he discover that Farmer Brown 's boy be a friend .
Always after he have leave , there be something good to eat near where he have be sit , for Farmer Brown 's boy bring corn and oat and sometimes a handful of wheat .
He know , and Mr. Quack know that he know , that somewhere near be a nest , but he do not try to find it much a he long to , for he know that would frighten and worry Mrs. Quack .
So the dear , precious secret of Mr. and Mrs. Quack be keep , for not even Paddy the Beaver know just where that nest be , and in due time , early one morning , Mrs. Quack proudly lead forth for their first swim ten downy , funny duckling .
-LSB- Illustration with caption : Those be happy day indeed for Mr. and Mrs. Quack in the pond of Paddy the Beaver . -RSB-
Oh , those be happy day indeed for Mr. and Mrs. Quack in the pond of Paddy the Beaver , and in their joy they quite forgot for a time the terrible journey which have bring them there .
But finally the Ducklings grow up , and when Jack Frost come in the fall , the whole family start on the long journey to the sunny Southland .
I hope they get there safely , do n't you ?
Among those whom Mr. and Mrs. Quack come to know very well while they live in the pond of Paddy the Beaver be that funny fellow who wear ring on his tail -- Bobby Coon .
In the next book I will tell you of some of Bobby 's adventure .

I HAPPY JACK SQUIRREL MAKES A FIND Happy Jack Squirrel have have a wonderful day .
He have find some big chestnut-trees that he have never see before , and which promise to give him all the nut he would want for all the next winter .
Now he be think of go home , for it be get late in the afternoon .
He look out across the open field where Mr. Goshawk have nearly catch him that morning .
His home be on the other side .
`` It 's a long way ` round , '' say Happy Jack to himself , `` but it be best to be safe and sure . ''
So Happy Jack start on his long journey around the open field .
Now , Happy Jack 's eye be bright , and there be very little that Happy Jack do not see .
So , a he be jump from one tree to another , he spy something down on the ground which excite his curiosity .
`` I must stop and see what that be , '' say Happy Jack .
So down the tree he run , and in a few minute he have find the queer thing , which have catch his eye .
It be smooth and black and white , and at one end it be very sharp with a tiny little barb .
Happy Jack find it out by prick himself with it .
`` Ooch , '' he cry , and drop the queer thing .
Pretty soon he notice there be a lot more on the ground .
`` I wonder what they be , '' say Happy Jack .
`` They do n't grow , for they have n't any root .
They be not thorn , for there be no plant from which they could come .
They be not alive , so what can they be ? ''
Now , Happy Jack 's eye be bright , but sometimes he do n't use them to the very best advantage .
He be so busy examine the queer thing on the ground that he never once think to look up in the top of the tree .
If he have , perhaps he would not have be so much puzzle .
As it be he just gather up three or four of the queer thing and start on again .
On the way he meet Peter Rabbit and show Peter what he have .
Now , you know Peter Rabbit be very curious .
He just could n't sit still , but must scamper over to the place Happy Jack Squirrel tell him about .
`` You 'd well be careful , Peter Rabbit ; they 're very sharp , '' shout Happy Jack .
But a usual , Peter be in too much of a hurry to heed what be say to him .
Lipperty-lipperty-lip , lipperty-lipperty-lip , go Peter Rabbit through the wood , as fast a his long leg would take him .
Then suddenly he squeal and sit down to nurse one of his foot .
But he be up again in a flash with another squeal louder than before .
Peter Rabbit have find the queer thing that Happy Jack Squirrel have tell him about .
One be stick in his foot , and one be in the white patch on the seat of his trouser .
II THE STRANGER FROM THE NORTH The Merry Little Breezes of Old Mother West Wind be excite .
Yes , Sir , they certainly be excite .
They have meet Happy Jack Squirrel and Peter Rabbit , and they be full of the news of the queer thing that Happy Jack and Peter Rabbit have find over in the Green Forest .
They hurry this way and that way over the Green Meadows and tell every one they meet .
Finally they reach the Smiling Pool and excitedly tell Grandfather Frog all about it .
Grandfather Frog smooth down his white and yellow waistcoat and look very wise , for you know that Grandfather Frog be very old .
`` Pooh , '' say Grandfather Frog .
`` I know what they be . ''
`` What ? ''
cry all the Merry Little Breezes together .
`` Happy Jack say he be sure they do not grow , for there be no strange plant over there . ''
Grandfather Frog open his big mouth and snap up a foolish green fly that one of the Merry Little Breezes blow over to him .
`` Chug-a-rum , '' say Grandfather Frog .
`` Things do not have to be on plant in order to grow .
Now I be sure that those thing grow , and that they do not grow on a plant . ''

ask one of them .

Presently , way up in the top of a big poplar , they find a stranger .
He be big than any of the little meadow people , and he have long sharp teeth with which he be strip the bark from the tree .
The hair of his coat be long , and out of it peep a thousand little spear just like the queer thing that Happy Jack and Peter Rabbit have tell them about .

`` Mornin ' , '' grunt the stranger in the treetop .

say one of the Merry Little Breezes politely .

III PRICKLY PORKY MAKES FRIENDS The Merry Little Breezes soon spread the news over the Green Meadows and through the Green Forest that a stranger have come from the North .
At once all the little meadow people and forest folk make some excuse to go over to the big poplar tree where the stranger be so busy eating .

He be a queer fellow , and he be so big , and his teeth be so sharp and so long , that his visitor keep their distance .

IV PETER RABBIT HAS SOME STARTLING NEWS Little Mrs. Peter Rabbit , who use to be Little Miss Fuzzytail , sit at the edge of the dear Old Briar-patch , anxiously look over towards the Green Forest .
She be worry .
There be no doubt about it .
Little Mrs. Peter be very much worry .
Why do n't Peter come home ?
She do wish that he would be content to stay close by the dear Old Briar-patch .
For her part , she could n't see why under the sun he want to go way over to the Green Forest .
He be always have dreadful adventure and narrow escape over there , and yet , in spite of all she could say , he would persist in go there .
She do n't feel easy in her mind one minute while he be out of her sight .
To be sure he always turn up all right , but she could n't help feeling that sometime his dreadful curiosity would get him into trouble that he could n't get out of , and so every time he go to the Green Forest , she be sure , absolutely sure , that she would never see him again .
Peter use to laugh at her and tell her that she be a foolish little dear , and that he be perfectly able to take care of himself .
Then , when he saw how worried she be , he would promise to be very , very careful and never do anything rash or foolish .
But he would n't promise not to go to the Green Forest .
No , Sir , Peter would n't promise that .
You see , he have so many friend over there , and there be always so much news to be gather that he just could n't keep away .
Once or twice he have induce Mrs. Peter to go with him , but she have be frighten almost out of her skin every minute , for it seem to her that there be danger lurk behind every tree and under every bush .
It be all very well for Chatterer the Red Squirrel and Happy Jack the Gray Squirrel , who could jump from tree to tree , but she do n't think it a safe and proper place for a sensible Rabbit , and she say so .
This particular morning she be unusually anxious .
Peter have be go all night .
Usually he be home by the time Old Mother West Wind come down from the Purple Hills and empty her child , the Merry Little Breezes , out of her big bag to play all day on the Green Meadows , but this morning Old Mother West Wind have be a long time go about her business , and still there be no sign of Peter .

V PETER RABBIT TELLS HIS STORY When Peter Rabbit could get his breath after his long hard run from the Green Forest to the dear Old Briar-patch , he have a wonderful story to tell .
It be all about a stranger in the Green Forest , and to have hear Peter tell about it , you would have think , a Mrs. Peter do , that it be a very terrible stranger , for it have no leg , and it have no head , and it have no tail .

VI PETER HAS TO TELL HIS STORY MANY TIMES Once you start a story you can not call it back ; It travel on and on and on and ever on , alack !
That be the reason why you should always be sure that a story you repeat be a good story .
Then you will be glad to have it travel on and on and on , and will never want to call it back .
But if you tell a story that be n't true or nice , the time be almost sure to come when you will want to call it back and can not .
You see story be just like river , -- they run on and on forever .
Little Mrs. Peter Rabbit know this , and that be why she advise Peter not to tell any one else the strange story he have tell her of the dreadful creature without leg or head or tail that have chase him in the Green Forest .
Peter knew by that that she do n't believe a word of it , but he be too tired and sleepy to argue with her then , so he settle himself comfortably for a nice long nap .
When Peter awake , the first thing he think of be the terrible creature he have see in the Green Forest .
The more he think about it , the more impossible it seem , and he do n't wonder that Mrs. Peter have advise him not to repeat it .
`` I wo n't , '' say Peter to himself .
`` I wo n't repeat it to a soul .
No one will believe it .
The truth be , I can hardly believe it myself .
I 'll just keep my tongue still . ''
But unfortunately for Peter , one of the Merry Little Breezes of Old Mother West Wind have hear Peter tell the story to Mrs. Peter , and it be such a wonderful and curious and unbelievable story that the Merry Little Breeze straightway repeat it to everybody he meet , and soon Peter Rabbit begin to receive caller who want to hear the story all over again from Peter himself .
So Peter be oblige to repeat it ever so many time , and every time it sound to him more foolish than before .
He have to tell it to Jimmy Skunk and to Johnny Chuck and to Danny Meadow Mouse and to Digger the Badger and to Sammy Jay and to Blacky the Crow and to Striped Chipmunk and to Happy Jack Squirrel and to Bobby Coon and to Unc ' Billy Possum and to Old Mr. Toad .
Now , strange to say , no one laugh at Peter , queer a the story sound .
You see , they all remember how they have laugh at him and make fun of him when he tell about the great footprint he have find deep in the Green Forest , and how late it have be proven that he really do see them , for they be make by Buster Bear who have come down from the Great Woods to live in the Green Forest .
Then it have be Peter 's turn to laugh at them .
So now , impossible a this new story sound , they do n't dare laugh at it .
`` I never heard of such a creature , '' say Jimmy Skunk , `` and I ca n't quite believe that there be such a one , but it be very clear to me that Peter have see something strange .
You know the old saying that he laugh best who laugh last , and I 'm not go to give Peter another chance to have the last laugh and say , ' I tell you so . ' ''
`` That be very true , '' reply Old Mr. Toad solemnly .
`` Probably Peter have see something out of the ordinary , and in his excitement he have exaggerate it .
The thing to do be to make sure whether or not there be a stranger in the Green Forest .

Why do n't you go up there and ask him , Jimmy Skunk ?
You 're not afraid of anybody or anything . ''
`` I will , '' reply Jimmy promptly , and off he start .

VII JIMMY SKUNK CALLS ON PRICKLY PORKY `` A plague upon Old Mr. Toad ! ''

VIII PRICKLY PORKY NEARLY CHOKES Hardly be Jimmy Skunk beyond sight and hearing after have make his call than Redeye the Vireo , whose home be in a tree just at the foot of the hill where Prickly Porky live , hear a very strange noise .

It never seem to enter his head that he be make other people happy just by be happy himself and say so .
At first he hardly notice the strange noise , but when he stop sing for a bit of a rest , he hear it very plainly , and it sound so very queer that he fly up the hill towards the place from which it seem to come , and there his bright eye soon discover Prickly Porky .

IX JIMMY SKUNK AND UNC ' BILLY POSSUM TELL DIFFERENT STORIES The little people of the Green Meadows and the Green Forest do n't know what to believe .

X UNC ' BILLY POSSUM TELLS JIMMY SKUNK A SECRET Be sure before you drop a friend That you 've do nothing to offend .

Unc ' Billy Possum say so , and he know .

Instead , he go to that friend , find out what the trouble be , explain it all away , and then do something nice .

XI WHAT HAPPENED TO REDDY FOX Reddy Fox wish with all his might that he have keep his tongue still about not be afraid to meet the strange creature that have give Peter Rabbit such a fright .
When he have boast that he would stop and find out all about it if he happen to meet it , he do n't have the least intention of do anything of the kind .
He be just idly boast and nothing more .
You see , Reddy be one of the great boaster in the Green Forest or on the Green Meadows .
He like to strut around and talk big .
But like most boaster , he be a coward at heart .
Unc ' Billy Possum know this , and that be why he dare Reddy to go the next morning to the foot of the hill where Prickly Porky the Porcupine live , and where Peter Rabbit have have his strange adventure , and where Unc ' Billy himself claim to have see the same strange creature without head , tail , or leg which have so frightened Peter .

You see , a number of little people have hear him boast and have hear Unc ' Billy dare him , and he know that if he do n't make good , he would never hear the end of it and would be call a coward by everybody .
Reddy do n't sleep at all well that afternoon , and when at dusk he start to hunt for his supper , he find that he have lose his appetite .
Instead of hunting , he spend most of the night in try to think of some good reason for not appear at Prickly Porky 's hill at daybreak .
But think a he would , he could n't think of a single excuse that would sound reasonable .

Very , very slowly , Reddy Fox begin to walk towards the hill where Prickly Porky live .

XIV REDDY FOX TRIES TO KEEP OUT OF SIGHT Never in all his life be Reddy Fox more uncomfortable in his mind .

he run away in fear . ''

XV OLD GRANNY FOX INVESTIGATES In-vest-i-gate be a great big word , but it meaning be very simple .
To in-vest-i-gate be to look into and try to find out all about something .
That be what old Granny Fox start to do after Reddy have tell her about the terrible fright he have have at the hill where Prickly Porky live .
Now old Granny Fox be very sly and smart and clever , a you all know .
Compared with her , Reddy Fox be almost stupid .
He may be a sly and smart and clever some day , but he have get a lot to learn before then .
Now if it have be Reddy who be go to investigate , he would have go straight over to Prickly Porky 's hill and look around and ask sly question , and everybody whom he meet would have know that he be try to find out something .
But old Granny Fox do nothing of the kind .
Oh , my , no !
She go about hunt her dinner just as usual and do n't appear to be pay the least attention to what be go on about her .
With her nose to the ground she run this way and run that way a if hunting for a trail .
She peer into old hollow log and look under little brush pile , and so , in course of time , she come to the hill where Prickly Porky live .
Now Reddy have tell Granny that the terrible creature that have so frightened him have roll down the hill at him , for he be at the bottom .
Granny have hear that the same thing have happen to Peter Rabbit and to Unc ' Billy Possum .
So instead of come to the hill along the hollow at the bottom , she come to it from the other way .
`` If there be anything there , I 'll be behind it instead of in front of it , '' she think shrewdly .
As she draw near where Prickly Porky live , she keep eye and ear wide open , all the time pretend to pay attention to nothing but the hunt for her dinner .
No one would ever have guess that she be think of anything else .
She run this way and that way all over the hill , but nothing out of the usual do she see or hear except one thing : she do find some queer mark down the hill a if something might have roll there .
She follow these down to the bottom , but there they disappear .
As she be trot home along the Lone Little Path through the Green Forest , she meet Unc ' Billy Possum .
No , she do n't exactly meet him , because he saw her before she saw him , and he promptly climb a tree .
`` Ah suppose yo'all heard of the terrible creature that scar Reddy almost out of his wit early this mo ` ning , '' say Unc ' Billy .
Granny stop and look up .
`` It do n't take much to scare the young and innocent , Mr. Possum , '' she reply .
`` I do n't believe all I hear .
I 've just be hunt all over the hill where Prickly Porky live , and I could n't find so much a a Wood Mouse for dinner .
Do you believe such a foolish tale , Mr. Possum ? ''
Unc ' Billy cough behind one hand .
`` Yes , Mrs. Fox , Ah confess Ah do have to believe it , '' he reply .
`` Yo ' see , Ah do see that thing mah own self , and Ah just naturally have to believe mah own eye . ''
`` Huh !
I 'd like to see it !
Maybe I 'd believe it then ! ''
snap Granny Fox .
`` The only time to see it be just at sun-up , '' reply Unc ' Billy .
`` Anybody that come along through that hollow at the foot of Brer Porky 's hill at sun-up be likely never to forget it .
Ah would n't do it again .
No , Sah , once be enough fo ' your Unc ' Billy . ''
`` Huh ! ''
snort Granny and trot on .
Unc ' Billy watch her out of sight and grin broadly .
`` As sho ' a Brer Sun get up to-morrow mo ` ning , Ol ' Granny Fox will be there , '' he chuckle .
`` Ah must get word to Brer Porky and Brer Skunk and Brer Rabbit . ''
XVI OLD GRANNY FOX LOSES HER DIGNITY Unc ' Billy Possum have pass the word along to Jimmy Skunk , Peter Rabbit , and Prickly Porky that old Granny Fox would be on hand at sun-up to see for herself the strange creature which have frighten Reddy Fox at the foot of the hill where Prickly Porky live .
How do Unc ' Billy know ?
Well , he just guess .
He be quite a shrewd and clever a Granny Fox herself , and when he tell her that the only time the strange creature everybody be talk about be see be at sun-up , he guess by the very way she sniff and pretend not to believe it at all that she would visit Prickly Porky 's hill the next morning .
`` The ol ' lady suspect that there be some trick , and we-uns have get to be very careful , '' warn Unc ' Billy , a he and his three friend put their head together in the early evening .
`` She be do bound to come snoop around before sun-up , '' he continue , `` and we-uns must be out of sight , all except Brer Porky .
She 'll come just the way she do this afternoon , -- from back of the hill instead of along the holler . ''
Unc ' Billy be quite right .
Old Granny Fox felt very sure that some one be play trick , so she do n't wait until jolly , round , red Mr. Sun be out of bed .
She be at the top of the hill where Prickly Porky live a full hour before sun-up , and there she sit down to wait .
She could n't see or hear anything in the least suspicious .
You see , Unc ' Billy Possum be quite out of sight , a he sit in the thick part of a hemlock-tree , and Peter Rabbit be sit perfectly still in a hollow log , and Jimmy Skunk be n't show so much a the tip of his nose , a he lay just inside the doorway of an old house under the root of a big stump .
Only Prickly Porky be to be see , and he seem to be asleep in his favorite tree .
Everything seem to be just a old Granny Fox have see it a hundred time before .
At last the Jolly Little Sunbeams begin to dance through the Green Forest , chase out the Black Shadows .
Redeye the Vireo awoke and at once begin to sing , a be his way , not even wait to get a mouthful of breakfast .
Prickly Porky yawn and grunt .
Then he climb down from the tree he have be sit in , walk slowly over to another , start to climb it , change his mind , and begin to poke around in the dead leaf .
Old Granny Fox arise and slowly stretch .
She glance at Prickly Porky contemptuously .
She have see him act in this stupid , uncertain way dozen of time before .
Then slowly , watch out sharply on both side of her , without appear to do so , she walk down the hill to the hollow at the foot .
Now old Granny Fox can be very dignified when she want to be , and she be now .
She do n't hurry the least little bit .
She carry her big , plumey tail just so .
And she do n't once look behind her , for she felt sure that there be nothing out of the way there , and to have do so would have be quite undignified .
She have reach the bottom of the hill and be walk along the hollow , smile to herself to think how easily some people be frighten , when her sharp ear catch a sound on the hill behind her .
She turn like a flash and then -- well , for a minute old Granny Fox be too surprised to do anything but stare .
There , roll down the hill straight towards her , be the very thing Reddy have tell her about .
At first Granny decide to stay right where she be and find out what this thing be , but the nearer it get , the stranger and more terrible it seem .
It be just a great ball all cover with dried leaf , and yet somehow Granny felt sure that it be alive , although she could see no head or tail or leg .
The nearer it get , the stranger and more terrible it seem .
Then Granny forget her dignity .
Yes , Sir , she forget her dignity .
In fact , she quite lose it altogether .
Granny Fox run just a Reddy have run !
XVII GRANNY FOX CATCHES PETER RABBIT Now listen to this little tale That deal somewhat with folly , And show how sometimes one may be A little bit too jolly .
No sooner be old Granny Fox out of sight , run a if she think that every jump might be her last , than Jimmy Skunk come out from the hole under a big stump where he have be hide , Peter Rabbit come out of the hollow log from which he have be peep , and Unc ' Billy Possum drop down from the hemlock-tree in which he have so carefully keep out of sight , and all three begin to dance around Prickly Porky , laugh a if they be try to split their side .

shout Jimmy Skunk .

Prickly Porky do n't say a word .
He just smile in a quiet sort of way a he slowly climb up to the top of the hill .
Now old Granny Fox have be badly frighten .
Who would n't have be at see a strange creature without head , tail , or legs roll down hill straight towards them ?
But Granny be too old and wise to run very far without cause .
She be hardly out of sight of the four little scamp who have be watch her when she stop to see if that strange creature be follow her .
It do n't take her long to decide that it be n't .
Then she do some quick thinking .

She waste no time think about it , but begin to steal back the way she have come .
Now , no one be light of foot than old Granny Fox , and no one know well how to keep out of sight .
From tree to tree she crawl , sometimes flat on her stomach , until at last she reach the foot of the hill where she have just have such a fright .
There be nothing to be see there , but up at the top of the hill she saw something that make a fierce , angry gleam come into her yellow eye .
Then she smile grimly .
`` The last laugh always be the best laugh , and this time I guess it be go to be mine , '' she say to herself .
Very slowly and carefully , so a not to so much a rustle a leaf , she begin to crawl around so a to come up on the back side of the hill .
Now what old Granny Fox have see be Peter Rabbit and Jimmy Skunk and Unc ' Billy Possum rolling over and over in the dried leaf , turn somersault , and shout and laugh , while Prickly Porky sit look on and smile .
Granny know well enough what be tickle them so , and she know too that they do n't dream but that she be still run away in fright .
At last they be so tired with their good time that they just have to stop for a rest .
`` Oh , dear , I 'm all out of breath , '' pant Peter , a he throw himself flat on the ground .
`` That be the funny thing I ever saw .
I wonder who we -- '' Peter do n't finish .
No , Sir , Peter do n't finish .
Instead , he give a frightened shriek a something red flash out from under a low-growing hemlock-tree close behind him , and two black paw pin him down , and sharp teeth catch him by the back of the neck .
Old Granny Fox have catch Peter Rabbit at last !
XVIII A FRIEND IN NEED IS A FRIEND INDEED The friendship which be truest , best , Is that which meet the trouble test .
No one really know who his best friend be until he get in trouble .
When everything be lovely and there be no sign of trouble anywhere , one may have ever and ever so many friend .
At least , it may seem so .
But let trouble come , and all too often these seem friend disappear a if by magic , until only a few , sometimes a very few , be leave .
These be the real friend , the true friend , and they be worth more than all the others put together .
Remember that if you be a true friend to any one , you will stand by him and help him , no matter what happen .
Sometimes it be almost worth while get into trouble just to find out who your real friend be .
Peter Rabbit find out who some of his true friend be when , because of his own carelessness , old Granny Fox catch him .
Peter have be in many tight place and have many terrible fright in his life , but never do he feel quite so helpless and hopeless a when he felt the black paw of old Granny Fox pin him down and Granny 's sharp teeth in the loose skin on the back of his neck .
All he could do be to kick with all his might , and kicking be quite useless , for Granny take great care to keep out of the way of those stout hind leg of his .
Many , many time Granny Fox have try to catch Peter , and always before Peter have be too smart for her , and have just make fun of her and laugh at her .
Now it be her turn to laugh , all because he have be careless and foolish .
You see , Peter have be so sure that Granny have have such a fright when she run away from the strange creature that roll down Prickly Porky 's hill at her that she would n't think of come back , and so he have just give himself up to enjoy Granny 's fright .
At Peter 's scream of fright , Unc ' Billy Possum scamper for the near tree , and Jimmy Skunk dodge behind a big stump .
You see , it be so sudden that they really do n't know what have happen .
But Prickly Porky , whom some people call stupid , make no move to run away .
He happen to be look at Peter when Granny catch him , and so he know just what it mean .
A spark of anger flash in his usually dull eye and for once in his life Prickly Porky move quickly .
The thousand little spear hide in his coat suddenly stand on end and Prickly Porky make a fierce little rush forward .

XIX JIMMY SKUNK TAKES WORD TO MRS. PETER When old Granny Fox find Prickly Porky , with his thousand little spear all pointing at her , stand between her and Peter Rabbit , she be the angry old Fox ever see .
She do n't dare touch Prickly Porky , for she know well enough what it would mean to get one of those sharp , barb little spear in her skin .

It be more than her temper , never of the best , could stand .

It make Peter shiver just to look at her .

`` No , you do n't ! ''
declare Jimmy Skunk .
`` You be go to stay right here where we can take care of you .

Peter try to insist on go home , but the others would n't hear of it , and Jimmy Skunk settle the matter by start for the dear Old Briar-patch .
He find little Mrs. Peter anxiously look towards the Green Forest for some sign of Peter .
`` Oh ! ''
she cry , `` you have come to bring me bad news .

But little Mrs. Peter be n't wholly satisfy .

Nothing that Jimmy could say have the least effect , and so at last he agree to take her to Peter .
And so , hop behind Jimmy Skunk , timid little Mrs. Peter Rabbit actually go into the Green Forest of which she be so much afraid , which show how brave love can be sometimes .
XX A PLOT TO FRIGHTEN OLD MAN COYOTE Mischief lead to mischief , for it be almost sure To never , never be content without a little more .
Now you would think that after Peter Rabbit 's very , very , narrow escape from the clutch of Old Granny Fox that Jimmy Skunk , Unc ' Billy Possum , Peter Rabbit , and Prickly Porky would have be satisfy with the prank they already have play .

You see , when danger be over , it be quickly forget .

Little Mrs. Peter be force to admit that she would , and after a little more teasing she finally agree to let them try their plan for give Old Man Coyote a scare .
Sammy Jay happen along just a Jimmy Skunk be start out to look for him , and when he be tell what be want of him , he agree to do his part .
You know Sammy be always ready for any mischief .

`` We-uns have have a lot of fun with Reddy and Granny Fox , '' say he , `` and now it seem to me that it be no more than fair to invite them over to see Old Man Coyote and what he will do when he first see the terrible creature that have frighten them so .
Granny know now that there be nothing to be afraid of , and perhaps she will forget her anger if she have a chance to see Old Man Coyote run away .
Yo ' know she be n't waste any love on him .
What do yo ' alls say ? ''
Peter and Mrs. Peter say `` No ! ''
right away , but Jimmy Skunk and Prickly Porky think it a good idea , and of course Sammy Jay be willing .
After a little , when it be once more point out to them how they would be perfectly safe in the old house behind the big stump , Peter and Mrs. Peter agree , and Sammy start off on his errand .
XXI SAMMY JAY DELIVERS HIS MESSAGE Sammy Jay have be the bearer of so many message that no one know good than he how to deliver one .
He know when to be polite , and no one can be more polite than he .
First he go over to the home of Reddy and Granny Fox and invite them to come over to the hill where Prickly Porky live and see the terrible creature which have frighten them so give Old Man Coyote a scare .
Both Reddy and Granny promptly say they would do nothing of the kind , that probably Sammy be engage in some kind of mischief , and that anyway they know that there be no such creature without head , legs , or tail , and though they have be fool once , they do n't propose to be fool again .
`` All right , '' reply Sammy , quite a if it make no difference to him .
`` You admit that smart a you be you be fool , and we think you might like to see the same thing happen to Old Man Coyote . ''
With this he fly on his way to the Green Meadows to look for Old Man Coyote , and a he fly he chuckle to himself .
`` They 'll be there , '' he mutter .

They 'll try to keep out of sight , but they 'll be there . ''
Sammy find Old Man Coyote take a sun-bath .
`` Good morning , Mr. Coyote .

XXII OLD MAN COYOTE LOSES HIS APPETITE Hardly be Sammy Jay out of sight , fly towards the Old Orchard , before Old Man Coyote start for the Green Forest .
He be very sharp , be Old Man Coyote , so sharp that it be not very often that he be fool .
If Sammy Jay have go to him and tell him what a splendid chance he would have to catch Peter Rabbit if he hurry up to the Green Forest right away , Old Man Coyote would have suspect a trick of some kind .
Sammy have be clever enough to know this .
So he have just mention in the most matter-of-fact way that he have see Peter over on Prickly Porky 's hill and that Peter appear to have be in trouble , so that he be too lame to go to his home in the dear Old Briar-patch .
There be n't even a hint that Old Man Coyote should go over there .
This be what make him sure that the news about Peter be probably true .
Now as soon a Sammy be sure that Old Man Coyote could n't see him , he head straight for the Green Forest and the hill where Prickly Porky , Jimmy Skunk , Unc ' Billy Possum , and Peter and Mrs. Peter Rabbit be wait .

`` I know they would be on hand , '' he chuckle .

So Unc ' Billy Possum climb a tree .
Jimmy Skunk crawl into a hollow log .

He saw Peter almost as soon a Peter saw him , and the instant he saw him , he stop as still a if he be make of stone .

Now of course Peter know just what be go on , and he take the great care not to get more than a couple of jump away from the old house under the big stump , where Mrs. Peter be hide and wish with all her might that she and Peter be back in the dear Old Briar-patch .

Old Man Coyote take one good look , hesitate , look again , and then turn tail and start for the Green Meadows as fast a his long leg would take him .

XXIII BUSTER BEAR GIVES IT ALL AWAY It be very clear that Old Man Coyote be n't think about his stomach just then , but about his leg and how fast they could go .
He have be half-way up the hill when he first saw the terrible creature without head , tail , or legs roll down straight at him .
He stop only long enough for one good look and then he start for the bottom of the hill as fast a he could make his leg go .
Now , it be a very bad plan to run fast down-hill .
Yes , Sir , it be a very bad plan .
You see , once you be start , it be not the easy thing in the world to stop .
And then again , you be quite likely to stub your toe .
This be what Old Man Coyote do .
He stub his toe and turn a complete somersault .
He look so funny that the little scamps watch him have all they could do to keep from shout right out .
Old Granny Fox and Reddy Fox , look on from a safe distance , do laugh .
You know they have not be friendly with Old Man Coyote since he come to live on the Green Meadows , and a they have themselves have a terrible fright when they first saw the strange creature , they rejoice in see him frightened .
But Old Man Coyote do n't stop for a little thing like a tumble .
Oh , my , no !
He just roll over on to his foot and be off again , hard than before .
Now there be very few people who can see behind them without turn their head a Peter Rabbit can , and Old Man Coyote be not one of them .
Trying to watch behind him , he do n't see where he be go , and the first thing he know he run bump into -- guess who !
Why , Buster Bear , to be sure .
Where Buster have come from nobody knew , but there he be , as big a life .
When Old Man Coyote run into him , he growl a deep , provoked growl and whirl around with one big paw raise to cuff whoever have so nearly upset him .
Old Man Coyote , more frightened than ever , yelp and run hard than before , so that by the time Buster Bear saw who it be who have run into him , he be safely out of reach and still run .
Then it be that Buster Bear first saw , roll down the hill , the strange creature which have so frightened Old Man Coyote .
Unc ' Billy Possum , Jimmy Skunk , Sammy Jay , Peter Rabbit and Mrs. Peter , watch from safe hiding place , wonder if Buster would run too .
If he do , it would be almost too good to be true .
But he do n't .
He look first at the strange creature roll down the hill , then at Old Man Coyote run as hard a ever he could , and his shrewd little eye begin to twinkle .
Then he begin to laugh .
`` Ha , ha , ha !

I. Granny Fox Gives Reddy a Scare Reddy Fox live with Granny Fox .
You see , Reddy be one of a large family , so large that Mother Fox have hard work to fee so many hungry little mouth and so she have let Reddy go to live with old Granny Fox .
Granny Fox be the wise , sly , smart fox in all the country round , and now that Reddy have grow so big , she think it about time that he begin to learn the thing that every fox should know .
So every day she take him hunt with her and teach him all the thing that she have learn about hunting : about how to steal Farmer Brown 's chicken without awaken Bowser the Hound , and all about the thousand and one way of fool a dog which she have learn .
This morning Granny Fox have take Reddy across the Green Meadows , up through the Green Forest , and over to the railroad track .
Reddy have never be there before and he do n't know just what to make of it .
Granny trot ahead until they come to a long bridge .
Then she stop .
`` Come here , Reddy , and look down , '' she command .
Reddy do a he be tell , but a glance down make him giddy , so giddy that he nearly fell .
Granny Fox grin .
`` Come across , '' say she , and run lightly across to the other side .
But Reddy Fox be afraid .
Yes , Sir , he be afraid to take one step on the long bridge .
He be afraid that he would fall through into the water or onto the cruel rock below .
Granny Fox run back to where Reddy sit .
`` For shame , Reddy Fox ! ''
say she .
`` What be you afraid of ?
Just do n't look down and you will be safe enough .
Now come along over with me . ''
But Reddy Fox hang back and beg to go home and whimper .
Suddenly Granny Fox sprang to her foot , a if in great fright .
`` Bowser the Hound !
Come , Reddy , come ! ''
she cry , and start across the bridge as fast a she could go .
Reddy do n't stop to look or to think .
His one idea be to get away from Bowser the Hound .
`` Wait , Granny !
Wait ! ''
he cry , and start after her as fast a he could run .
He be in the middle of the bridge before he remember it at all .
When he be at last safely across , it be to find old Granny Fox sit down laugh at him .
Then for the first time Reddy look behind him to see where Bowser the Hound might be .
He be nowhere to be see .
Could he have fall off the bridge ?
`` Where be Bowser the Hound ? ''
cry Reddy .
`` Home in Farmer Brown 's dooryard , '' reply Granny Fox dryly .
Reddy star at her for a minute .
Then he begin to understand that Granny Fox have simply scar him into run across the bridge .
Reddy felt very cheap , very cheap indeed .
`` Now we 'll run back again , '' say Granny Fox .
And this time Reddy do .
II .
Granny Shows Reddy a Trick Every day Granny Fox lead Reddy Fox over to the long railroad bridge and make him run back and forth across it until he have no fear of it whatever .
At first it have make him dizzy , but now he could run across at the top of his speed and not mind it in the least .
`` I do n't see what good it do to be able to run across a bridge ; anyone can do that ! ''

Granny Fox smile .
`` Do you remember the first time you try to do it ? ''
